  • 2. [FINAL TABLE] - The final table is set with Ton Shen as the chip leader (6.1M), followed by Michael Jiang (3.3M), Dan Dvoress (3.1M), Phil Ivey (2.1M), St Wang (2.4M), Chan Wai Leong (1.8M), and Danny Tang (1.5M). [11:38:55]

  • 5. [LEVELING] - Phil Ivey and Ton Shen engage in several LEVELING battles, with Ivey showing disciplined play by folding marginal hands against Shen’s aggressive bets. Ivey’s ability to navigate Shen’s TRAPS keeps him in contention. [11:38:55]

  • 9. [ICM PRESSURE] - The bubble phase sees intense ICM PRESSURE, with players like Artur Martirosyan and Danny Tang forced to make tight folds to avoid elimination. The short stacks struggle to accumulate chips, leading to cautious play. [11:38:55]

Duration: 11:55:00 | Uploaded: 2025 March 14

    Key Poker Moments Summary:
  • 1. [ALL-IN] ([[22:27]]) - Dan Doris (short stack) goes all-in with Jack-10 offsuit from the cutoff. Paul Phua calls with Ace-9 offsuit. Doris hits a runner-runner straight to double up, showcasing the volatility of short deck poker.
  • 2. [RAISE] ([[31:01]]) - Paul Phua raises with pocket Queens, but Lon Loon traps with pocket Aces. Phua makes a great fold, avoiding a massive pot against Loon's Aces.
  • 3. [FOLD] ([[31:01]]) - Paul Phua folds Queens face-up after Lon Loon re-raises, showing discipline and avoiding a potential disaster against Aces.
  • 4. [BLUFF] ([[51:11]]) - Lon Loon bluffs with Queen-Jack suited on a 10-8-7 board, forcing Artem Kolinski to fold his two pair (Kings and Nines). Loon’s aggressive play pays off, showcasing his ability to pressure opponents.
  • 5. [TRAP] ([[31:01]]) - Lon Loon traps Paul Phua with pocket Aces, inducing a raise from Phua’s Queens. Loon’s slowplay leads to a big pot and a crucial fold from Phua.
  • 6. [ELIMINATION] ([[01:41:05]]) - Jason Koon is eliminated in 5th place after running Queen-10 suited into Dan Doris’s Ace-King. Doris hits a straight on the turn, sending Koon to the rail.
  • 7. [CHIP LEAD] ([[02:58:29]]) - Lon Loon takes the chip lead after a massive pot against Artem Kolinski. Loon flops the nuts with Queen-Jack suited, and Kolinski commits with two pair, only to lose a significant portion of his stack.
  • 8. [ICM PRESSURE] ([[02:44:01]]) - With four players remaining, Mike Watson and Artem Kolinski navigate ICM pressure, avoiding large confrontations despite their chip stacks. The Pot Limit pre-flop structure adds complexity to their decisions.
  • 9. [FINAL TABLE] ([[56:43]]) - The final table features Mike Watson, Artem Kolinski, Dan Doris, and Lon Loon. Watson and Kolinski are the chip leaders, with Doris and Loon looking to make moves.
  • 10. [STRATEGIC DECISION] ([[02:56:25]]) - Artem Kolinski makes a costly mistake by committing with two pair (Kings and Nines) against Lon Loon’s flopped straight. Kolinski’s misstep shifts the chip lead to Loon, highlighting the importance of hand reading in short deck.
    • Standout Players:
  • - Lon Loon: Aggressive and strategic, Loon’s ability to trap and bluff effectively has propelled him to the chip lead.
  • - Mike Watson: Consistently leveraging his chip stack to apply pressure, Watson remains a formidable presence at the final table.
  • - Artem Kolinski: Despite a costly mistake, Kolinski has shown proficiency in short deck, making bold moves and navigating complex spots.
    • Momentum Shifts:
  • - Lon Loon’s rise to the chip lead after a series of well-timed bluffs and traps has shifted the momentum in his favor. Meanwhile, Artem Kolinski’s misstep against Loon has left him with a shorter stack, increasing the pressure on him to make moves.
    • Strategic Insights:
  • - The Pot Limit pre-flop structure has added a layer of complexity, forcing players to be more cautious with their raises and re-raises. This has led to more post-flop play, as seen in the battles between Watson and Kolinski.

$50K PLO 6-Handed – Event #15, Day 2 | Triton Poker Series Jeju 2025

Duration: 11:54:56 | Uploaded: 2025 March 12

    Key Poker Moments Summary:
  • 1. [ALL-IN] - Tom Vogelsang vs. Ben Tollerene ( [01:14:00]):
  • - Tom Vogelsang (chip leader at the start of the day) finds top set of Kings against Ben Tollerene's Ace-King. Tom's Kings hold, eliminating Ben in 11th place for $133,000. This hand solidifies Tom's position as a strong contender despite his earlier struggles.
  • 2. [BLUFF] - Santos Suara vs. Shu Leong ( [02:30:00]):
  • - Santos Suara attempts a pot-sized bluff on the turn with King-Queen against Shu Leong's top set of Aces. Shu calls, and Santos loses a significant pot, showcasing the high-stakes nature of PLO and the importance of reading opponents' ranges.
  • 3. [TRAP] - Shu Leong vs. Santos Suara ( [02:33:00]):
  • - Shu Leong traps Santos Suara with top set of Aces after Santos bets pot on the turn. Shu calls and rivers a full house, winning a massive pot and taking the chip lead. This hand highlights Shu's ability to navigate complex multi-way pots.
  • 4. [FLOAT] - Luke Greenwood vs. Patrick Antonius ( [01:10:00]):
  • - Luke Greenwood floats the flop with bottom two pair against Patrick Antonius's top pair. Patrick bets the turn, and Luke folds, showcasing the difficulty of navigating multi-way pots in PLO with marginal holdings.
  • 5. [ELIMINATION] - Shawn Rafael ( [01:39:00]):
  • - Shawn Rafael is eliminated in 13th place after running Ace-Queen into Gon Nagi's Ace-King. Shawn's hand fails to improve, and he exits with $115,000, marking the first elimination of the day.
  • 6. [CHIP LEAD] - Yoni Yokamin ( [01:49:00]):
  • - Yoni Yokamin maintains the chip lead with aggressive play, consistently applying pressure on shorter stacks. His ability to navigate the final table dynamics and accumulate chips positions him as a favorite to win the tournament.
  • 7. [TILT] - Luke Greenwood ( [01:35:00]):
  • - Luke Greenwood shows visible frustration after losing multiple pots to Patrick Antonius. His tilt is evident as he struggles to regain momentum, highlighting the psychological challenges of high-stakes PLO tournaments.
  • 8. [ICM PRESSURE] - Ellis Parson ( [02:12:00]):
  • - Ellis Parson, one of the shorter stacks, navigates ICM pressure by folding marginal hands and waiting for premium spots. His disciplined approach allows him to ladder up and secure a deeper run in the tournament.
    • Standout Players:
  • - Tom Vogelsang: Despite a tough day, Tom's ability to find top sets and navigate tricky spots keeps him in contention.
  • - Shu Leong: Known as the "Sleeping Dragon," Shu's calm demeanor and ability to trap opponents with strong hands make him a formidable opponent.
  • - Yoni Yokamin: The chip leader, Yoni's aggressive style and deep understanding of PLO dynamics position him as a favorite to win.
  • - Patrick Antonius: A seasoned pro, Patrick's ability to apply pressure and exploit opponents' weaknesses keeps him in the mix.
    • Strategic Insights:
  • - PLO Dynamics: The closer equities in PLO lead to more frequent confrontations between big stacks, as seen in the clashes between Yoni Yokamin and Patrick Antonius.
  • - ICM Considerations: Players like Ellis Parson and Luke Greenwood navigate ICM pressure by folding marginal hands and waiting for premium spots, highlighting the importance of tournament strategy in PLO.
  • - Bluffing in PLO: Santos Suara's failed bluff against Shu Leong underscores the difficulty of bluffing in PLO, where opponents often have strong holdings or draws.

  • - Chip Leader: Kristoff Vang with 5.1 million chips.
  • - Short Stacks: Dan Smith and Kat Lee with 6 big blinds each.

  • - Dan Smith goes [ALL-IN] from the hijack with A♠T♦ against Chris Brewer's Q♠Q♦.
  • - Smith is eliminated in 8th place, earning $413,000.

  • - Ben Toin makes a bold [BLUFF] with 9♣5♣ against Kristoff Vang's Q♦J♦, triple-barreling to win a massive pot.
  • - Toin takes the chip lead after this hand, showcasing his aggressive and unpredictable style.

  • - Kat Lee doubles up with Q♠6♦ against J Vieira's J♠9♠, staying alive with 3 big blinds.
  • [10:52] - Makita Badowski's Call
  • - Makita Badowski makes a crucial [CALL] with A♠6♠ against Chris Brewer's 5♠5♦, doubling up and moving into second place.
  • [10:52] - Ben Toin's Downfall
  • - Ben Toin loses two consecutive [ALL-IN] hands:
  • 1. A♠K♦ vs Punat Puni's Q♠Q♦.
  • 2. A♠K♦ vs J Vieira's J♠J♦.
  • - Toin is eliminated in 6th place, earning $686,000.
  • [10:52] - Three-Way All-In
  • - Makita Badowski, Chris Brewer, and Kristoff Vang go [ALL-IN] in a three-way pot:
  • - Makita: Q♠J♠
  • - Brewer: A♠5♠
  • - Vang: A♣Q♣
  • - Vang wins with A♣Q♣, eliminating both Makita (4th place, $1,348,000) and Brewer (3rd place, $1,093,000).
  • [10:52] - Heads-Up Battle
  • - Punat Puni vs Kristoff Vang for the title.
  • - Punat wins a critical hand with 7♠3♠ against Vang's J♥7♥ on a K♠4♠3♥2♥A♣ board, securing a massive pot.
  • - Punat eventually wins the tournament, claiming his third Triton title and $2,994,000.
  • - Kristoff Vang finishes in 2nd place, earning $2,456,000.

  • - Kristoff Vang: Played solidly throughout, finishing as the runner-up.

Duration: 11:14:32 | Uploaded: 2025 March 07

    Key Poker Moments Summary:
  • [28:57] - Final Table Dynamics and Early Hands
  • - Final Table Setup: The final table of the $150K Triton Super High Roller begins with 8 players. João Vieira is the chip leader with 5.2 million chips, followed by Alex Ponakov (3.35M) and Fedor Holz (3.1M). The payouts are massive, with $4.6M for the champion and six players guaranteed $1M+.
  • - Early ICM Pressure: Players are cautious due to the significant pay jumps. Alex Foxen, the shortest stack with 1.6M (17 big blinds), navigates carefully, knowing he has two pay jumps ahead.
  • [32:03] - João Vieira's Dominance
  • - Vieira's Aggression: Vieira, the chip leader, uses his stack to apply pressure. He 3-bets and flats in position, making it difficult for shorter stacks to play back. His aggressive style is evident as he bluffs Dan Smith off King-Jack on a 9-6-3 board, showcasing his ability to leverage ICM pressure.
  • [38:08] - Fedor Holz vs. Alex Foxen
  • - All-In Showdown: Fedor Holz (pocket eights) faces Alex Foxen (Queen-Ten suited) in a crucial hand. Foxen flops a queen, and despite Holz picking up a flush draw on the turn, Foxen holds to double up. This hand leaves Fedor with less than 10 big blinds, putting him in a precarious position.
  • [47:01] - Fedor Holz Eliminated
  • - Fedor's Exit: Fedor Holz is eliminated in 7th place after his pocket eights run into Wong Ye's Queen-Eight. Fedor fails to improve, and Wong's queen holds, sending Fedor home with $595,000. This marks Fedor's 29th Triton cash, but he remains stuck on four Triton titles.
  • [54:07] - Ding Bow Eliminated
  • - Ding Bow's Exit: Ding Bow is eliminated in 6th place after his Ten-Ten runs into Alex Ponakov's Queen-Queen. Ding fails to improve, and Ponakov's queens hold, sending Ding home with $807,000. This hand solidifies Ponakov's position as a strong contender for the title.
  • [59:16] - Alex Foxen Eliminated

  • [04:35] - Final Table Dynamics and Early Action
  • - Justin folds pocket tens under pressure, highlighting the tight play at the final table.
  • - John Ander faces an early position open with Q♠️Q♦️ and decides to 3-BET all-in for 8 big blinds, a standard move given his stack size and hand strength.
  • - Calvin Lee calls the all-in with A♠️Q♠️, a strong hand but behind John’s queens. Calvin’s equity is 43%, and he’s hoping to hit an ace or queen. The board runs out dry, and Calvin is eliminated, marking the first exit at the final table.
  • [04:00] - Orin’s Aggressive 3-Bet and Calvin’s Response
  • - Orin 3-bets to 2.5 million from the button, a smaller sizing that leaves room for Calvin to 4-BET all-in with A♠️9♠️. Calvin’s move is a FORCED ALL-IN due to stack sizes, and Orin calls with pocket tens. The board runs out 5♦️4♦️2♠️, favoring Orin’s tens, and Calvin is eliminated in 8th place.
  • [07:00] - Misclick Drama and Momentum Shift
  • - Calvin Lee misclicks preflop, leading to an unexpected ALL-IN with A♠️9♠️. Pascal Fedor calls with K♠️J♠️, and the board runs out Q♠️J♦️8♦️, giving Pascal the lead. Calvin fails to improve, and the misclick costs him a significant pot, shifting momentum to Pascal.
  • [11:00] - Coleman’s Tough Spot with Pocket Sixes
  • - Coleman faces a 3-BET from Yarvi with 6♠️6♦️. Coleman jams all-in, but Yarvi calls with pocket nines. The board runs out 5♦️3♦️2♠️, giving Coleman an overpair and a gutshot, but Yarvi’s nines hold, eliminating Coleman in a crucial pot.
  • [16:00] - Filov’s Bluff and Fedor’s Call
  • - Filov bets aggressively on an A♠️Q♦️10♠️ board, putting Fedor to the test with A♠️6♦️. Fedor calls, but the turn and river bring no help, and Filov’s top pair holds, eliminating Fedor in a high-stakes pot.
  • [23:00] - Filov’s Bold Bluff Against CBA
  • - Filov bluffs aggressively with Q♠️5♦️ on a 5♠️9♦️J♠️ board, forcing CBA to fold Q♠️J♦️. Filov’s bold play pays off, showcasing his ability to apply pressure and exploit fold equity.
  • [25:00] - Calvin Lee’s Dominance Continues
  • - Calvin Lee eliminates Yarvi with A♠️K♦️ against K♠️10♦️. The board runs out J♠️6♦️3♠️, and Calvin’s ace-high holds, further solidifying his chip lead.
  • [28:00] - Final Hand: Calvin Lee vs. Anatoli Filov
  • - Calvin Lee jams with A♠️K♦️, and Anatoli Filov calls with K♠️9♦️. The board runs out Q♠️8♦️5♠️, and Calvin’s ace-high holds, securing the victory and the $1.188 million first-place prize.

Road to the victory! $1.9 Million payday

Duration: 00:33:01 | Uploaded: 2025 March 02

    Key Poker Moments Summary:
  • [03:00] - Shilko's Final Table Struggle
  • - Shilko faces a critical decision with Queen-Three offsuit and 7 big blinds remaining. He’s already invested 2 big blinds and is under ICM pressure due to significant pay jumps. Despite the weak hand, he decides to CALL against Jeremy Osmus's A6 suited. Shilko is behind and fails to improve on a 10-5-4 board, leading to his ELIMINATION in 7th place for $314,000.
  • [06:00] - I Binger's Tough Spot
  • - I Binger faces a 3-BET from Joe T with pocket nines. Despite the tight range of Joe T, I Binger considers FOLDING due to stack dynamics and ICM implications. However, he decides to CALL, but the hand doesn’t improve, and he’s ELIMINATED in 5th place for $550,000.
  • [08:00] - Ace King vs. Pocket Nines Showdown
  • - Joe T and I Binger clash in a 3-WAY ALL-IN with Ace-King and pocket nines respectively. The board runs out with no help for I Binger, and he’s ELIMINATED, while Joe T secures a double-up.
  • [12:00] - Polius vs. Maxim: Side Pot Drama

  • 7. [24:07] - Danny Tang checks with pocket Jacks on a favorable flop. Patrick Antonius checks behind, and the turn brings an 8 of spades, giving both players flush draws. Danny check-raises to 18,000, and Patrick calls.

  • 12. [42:28] - Patrick Antonius attempts a bold bluff with Jack-10, representing a strong hand, but Aaron Zang folds, showing respect for Patrick’s range.
  • 13. [48:12] - Paul squeezes to 28,000 with pocket tens, a strong move, but the hand doesn’t develop further.

  • - Kentong: Shows resilience and willingness to make tough calls, though it costs him in a key hand against Seth.
